< Text>
I have to admit that I made fun of this place for setting cheap ass wine, and to my surprise, it was actually my favorite out of the 4 wineries that we went to that day. The tasting is super cheap or if you buy a bottle (which is super cheap as well), you get the tasting for free. Either way, you win. I like the wines here as they are sweeter and taste more like juice. I love sweet wines (mainly moscato) and this place totally supplied what I was looking for.

Overall, I will never call this "cheap ass wine" again. And even if it is, who cares? It's delicious!</Text>

I enjoyed my visit to one of California's biggest wineries ... no problems ... but the reason I am not giving Sutter Home a high rating is because the experience felt like it was mass-market and mainstream, as opposed to a boutique or off-the-beaten path kind of experience.  Sutter Home wines are so popular and commonplace that they are served on some airlines in tiny bottles.  I regard their wines as some of the early wines that made California wines famous, but in my experience, people don't buy Sutter Home wines much anymore, except perhaps for big institutional or corporate users.  But I gotta give Sutter Home credit for helping get this industry established and thriving in Napa Valley.  The tour group I was with was given a talk in the building, and then some tastings while standing in a gift shop, and we were invited to step outside (beautiful day) to lounge on the lawn and near the old Victorian house which is adjacent to the tasting room facility.  We did not see any of the other buildings or anything else on the property.  The tasting room building is right up against the busy highway, detracting from any sense of natural surroundings.  Everything was neat, professional, nice and normal ..... but special? ?< /review>

<GmapID>0x808450d1dc86996d:0xd7423a7f63ca22ff<//GmapID>< Text>
BETWEEN THE REVIEWS w/ Rodney S

Q)  Rodney, while you were in Napa, did you experience any wine tastings?
A)  Yes, Rodney, I did!  On my tight schedule, I went to a Grand Pour wine tasting at the Westin Verasa Napa, with the following day a visit to Sutter Home Winery.

Q)  Were there appetizers to munch on?
A)  Rodney, Sutter Home had a sumptuous charcuterie spread to go along with their menagerie of wine, which included goat & sheep cheese, figs & apricots.

Q)  How were the wine tastings, Rodney?
A)  The wine kept flowing to the visitor's content.  So much so, a young woman threw up on the shuttle bus back to the hotel.  I'm not really a drinker, perhaps indulging a couple times a year, so I enjoyed the sweeter libations, like their sangria & sparkling prosecco.  I also had tastings of Sutter Home reserve wine, not sold in stores, such as their sangiovese.

Q)  What else did you do at Sutter Home Winery?
A)  After helping ourselves to charcuterie & glass after glass of wine, we were entertained by a private concert in the round.  Underneath a party canopy, we enjoyed the musical talents of Zach Heckendorf, Brendan James & Drake White.

A fun photobooth provided the poops & giggles

Q)  Rodney, do you recommend visiting Sutter Home Winery for a tasting?
A)  Absolutely, Rodney!  The staff were friendly & hospitable during the couple hours we spent at the winery.  The grounds were beautiful to meander about in & I found a greater appreciation for wine.  Although Sutter Home is considered an economy class wine, the Sutter Home Winery wine tasting was first class all the way.<//Text>

<text>When my October 2015 scores came out, I was overjoyed to find that I got a 2310 on the SAT reasoning test. Because of Zenith, I was able to develop in my weakest areas and feel confident in myself on the day of test. In fact, I went from a 700 in writing (previously my weakest section) to an 800.

While its score guarantee is appealing and the class really does provide students with the resources to achieve their desired scores, Zenith's advanced class ultimately gives you what you put into it. To ensure the 2300+ score guarantee, Zenith requires students to maintain a 90% quiz average (such quizzes are given weekly in class and test strategy knowledge and vocab). If a 90% average seems hard for you to attain, don't worry. If you study a lot and still aren't quite breaking 90's on quizzes, chances are you're still retaining the strategy knowledge necessary to crack 2300 on the real test. This was the case for me.

Zenith provides a huge arsenal of resources for its students, including dozens of practice tests, exhaustive strategy guides for each section, and online explanation videos for hard test questions. As a student in the advanced class, you will be expected to work hard. My class met for three hours every week for eight weeks (I believe there are other timing options, but I'm fairly sure all advanced classes meet for 24 total hours), and required around 6 hours of class-related homework per week (for me 4 hours was the least in a week, 8 hours was the most).

So yes, the work is pretty grueling.

However, my class teacher, Grayson, who also owns the company, was a big help. Class time always flew by surprisingly fast because he used the time so productively. Grayson helped me become more confident in my critical reading analysis skills by grilling me on the questions I got wrong, telling me to find the evidence in the passage, because, as I learned, the evidence is always somewhere in the passage, you just have to look. Grayson motivated me to be smart, study hard and "beat" the SAT, and for that, I am very grateful to him and highly recommend him if you choose to attend a Zenith class.

My parents and I were and still are very satisfied with my score and we have Zenith to thank. I don't know where I'd be without Zenith :~).<//text>< pics>

< Review>
I am a straight-A student and as a result I already had a pretty high SAT (2050) and ACT (32) score when I came to Zenith Tutoring. However, thanks to Grayson, I managed to increase my scores to 2250 and 35, respectively, after only a month of tutoring. What makes my SAT score even more impressive, is that I had a horrible headache during the second half of the test and was practically guessing on the last few sections.

Grayson is unlike any other tutor that I have ever met. He truly believes in your success and will not stop until you get a perfect score on EVERY section. When I first took my SAT I got a 590 on the reading section. After a summer of learning vocab and reading through countless SAT Prep books (6, I believe) I managed to raise it a mere 30 points to a 620. Needless to say I was unhappy, but I was never good at English anyway and eventually came to terms with my low score. Consequently, when I came to Zenith Tutoring I told Grayson that there was nothing he or I could do about my Reading score‚ÄîI was already at the top of my reach‚Äîand that we would be better off focusing on Math and Writing. Thankfully he didn't believe me. Today I am the proud owner of a 770 Reading sub-score, an unfathomable amount that I could have never even have hoped for.

I could see a similar trend in the scores of the other students in Grayson's SAT class: people with extremely low reading or writing or math scores, people who would have been happy with only a 700 on that particularly hard section, managed to get close to, if not exactly, a perfect score.

Finally, unlike any other tutors that I tried, in Grayson's class we always started on time and were working for the entire session. There were no "tell me about yourself" questions that last for half an hour or long anecdotes that had absolutely nothing to do with my SAT/ACT. Every second of Grayson's class was spent on track.

I would definitely recommend Zenith Tutoring to anyone who wants to get a good score on their SAT, ACT, or simply need help on a hard AP class. And I will surely be coming back to get help with my college application essays.<//Review>
